  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_74904aa7-5a37-4778-928c-447b896c0d14'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer5888632525884586281">The missing dead call to Violet. They want to be found. Violet can sense the echoes of those who've been murdered and the matching imprint that clings to their killers. Only those closest to her know what she is capable of, but when she discovers the body of a young boy she also draws the attention of the FBI, threatening her entire way of life.<br/><br/>As Violet works to keep her </span>
  <span id="freeText5888632525884586281" style="display:none">The missing dead call to Violet. They want to be found. Violet can sense the echoes of those who've been murdered and the matching imprint that clings to their killers. Only those closest to her know what she is capable of, but when she discovers the body of a young boy she also draws the attention of the FBI, threatening her entire way of life.<br /><br />As Violet works to keep her morbid ability a secret, she unwittingly becomes the object of a dangerous obsession. Normally, she'd turn to her best friend, Jay, except now that they are officially a couple, the rules of their relationship seem to have changed. And with Jay spending more and more time with his new friend Mike, Violet is left with too much time on her hands as she wonders where things went wrong. But when she fills the void by digging into Mike's tragic family history, she stumbles upon a dark truth that could put everyone in danger.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There is definitely more character development in this book than in the first! If you enjoyed the story between Violet & Jay, then I'd highly suggest <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There is definitely more character development in this book than in the first! If you enjoyed the story between Violet &amp; Jay, then I'd highly suggest reading it! Also, to me, it seems like there will be a couple of new characters added in to make the story more enticing. This book has definitely left me wanting to see how their stories all unfold, as well :)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135186779?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135186779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer566660594250443051">Me: So, Violet, congrats on not getting killed and all by that serial killer in your first big adventure.<br/><br/>Violet: I’m just so happy Jay was there. I was soooo scared when I thought he was dead. I mean, what would life be without him?<br/><br/>Me: Yeah, I guess that would’ve been bad. Anyway, you learned something from that experience, right? Like…to not wander off by yourself? In the dark? Where dead bodies are?<br/><br/>Violet: You sound just like Jay. This is why I don’t tell him things. And then he gets mad at me</span>
  <span id="freeText566660594250443051" style="display:none">Me: So, Violet, congrats on not getting killed and all by that serial killer in your first big adventure.<br /><br />Violet: I’m just so happy Jay was there. I was soooo scared when I thought he was dead. I mean, what would life be without him?<br /><br />Me: Yeah, I guess that would’ve been bad. Anyway, you learned something from that experience, right? Like…to not wander off by yourself? In the dark? Where dead bodies are?<br /><br />Violet: You sound just like Jay. This is why I don’t tell him things. And then he gets mad at me, just like you do.<br /><br />Me: Because you’re being dumb.<br /><br />Violet: I am NOT. The dead bodies <i>call</i> to me! I can’t <i>help</i> it! <br /><br />Me: But you could tell <i>Jay</i> before you ran off alone in the vicinity of where a killer has been, right?<br /><br />Violet: He’d just tell my parents or my police chief uncle or something. I have to do this by myself. I can’t tell Jay. Even though he <i>is</i> perfect.<br /><br />Me: Why?<br /><br />Violet: Well, he’s really hot—even random waitresses hit on him and give him free stuff, which is <i>really</i> annoying, actually. And he’s so sweet and we’ve been best friends since <i>forever</i> and he’s an <i>amazing</i> kisser—<br /><br />Me: No, no, no. I don’t give a crap about Jay and his perfectness. I’m talking about <i>why</i> you have to uncover the bodies by yourself. You ended up calling the police about the body at the docks anyway, right?<br /><br />Violet: Yeah, but—<br /><br />Me: And you didn’t even help them solve that murder! In fact, the body at the docks was just a decoy plot wasn’t it? You didn’t do <i>anything</i> about it besides find the body. <br /><br />Violet: Maybe, but—<br /><br />Me: And you had someone in contact with the FBI aiding you when you went after the second body! Why didn’t you call them?<br /><br />Violet: Well…<br /><br />Me: Well, what? <br /><br />Violet: *mumbles* The bodies call to me…<br /><br />Me: Do the bodies make you immune to common sense?<br /><br />Violet: You really <i>do</i> sound like Jay. <br /><br />Me: And about Jay…why did you get in a fight with him, again?<br /><br />Violet: He didn’t support me when I thought that his new bestie’s sister was the one who had left a dead cat on my doorstep.<br /><br />Me: So…he didn’t believe you right away. Once. After you had shown a continuous lack of judgment and common sense. And you broke up with him after doing nothing but talk about how perfect and wonderful he was and how he was your best friend and you were soulmates or whatever?<br /><br />Violet: He’s my boyfriend and best friend! He should trust me and support me! He’s supposed to believe in me no matter what!<br /><br />Me: After you got into a fight over this, did he try to call you?<br /><br />Violet: Yes.<br /><br />Me: Did he try to apologize?<br /><br />Violet: Yes.<br /><br />Me: Did you just ignore him and avoid him?<br /><br />Violet: Yes.<br /><br />Me: Did you ever once try to have a mature conversation about how you were feeling?<br /><br />Violet: No.<br /><br />Me: So why did you think you were mature enough to be having sex?<br /><br />Violet: It’s not a question of maturity. I can’t control myself around Jay. I mean, he was trying to take things slow. He kept telling me no, can you believe that?<br /><br />Me: Hmm…teenage boy consistently turning down a girl trying to jump him every time they’re alone. Does Jay happen to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight" rel="nofollow noopener"> sparkle in the sun?</a><br /><br />Violet: What are you talking about?<br /><br />Me: Nothing, private joke. Sometimes I get so bored I have to amuse myself.<br /><br />Violet: Okaaay…<br /><br />Me: By the way, do you actually <i>like</i> Chelsea?<br /><br />Violet: She’s my friend!<br /><br />Me: So you say. But you constantly describe her as annoying, loud, bratty, selfish, obnoxious and shallow. You kinda barely tolerate her.<br /><br />Violet: She can be fun as long as no one else is around.<br /><br />Me: Are you sure you don’t just hang out with her so you feel better about yourself in comparison?<br /><br />Violet: I don’t know what you’re talking about.<br /><br />Me: How about some quotes: “even Chelsea’s car was obnoxious.” And, my personal favorite: “Chelsea…looked crestfallen, like she was shriveling, and Violet actually felt sorry for her friend, something that took her entirely by surprise. But as bad as she felt for Chelsea, Violet wasn’t about to turn down the opportunity to be alone with Jay.” Are you actually that cold that you are surprised you feel bad when your friend is crushed? Or just that horny?<br /><br />Violet: You don’t understand. Chelsea’s annoying. And Jay is Jay.<br /><br />Me: I thought Chelsea was your friend<br /><br />Violet: Jay’s my best friend.<br /><br />Me: Yeah, okay. And you’re really possessive. You’re jealous Jay has male friends.<br /><br />Violet: Jay is my boyfriend! We should spend all our time together!<br /><br />Me: Except when you get pissed off at him and refuse to speak with him and go all drama queen.<br /><br />Violet: STOP BEING MEAN TO ME! JAY IS MY ONE AND ONLY AND SHOULD NEVER DOUBT ME <i>EVER</i>, OKAY?!?<br /><br />Me: I’m almost done here, then you can do nothing but run headlong into danger and obsess about Jay. I just want to say I think you should hang out with Rafe more. He was pretty cool.<br /><br />Violet: Are you trying to keep me and Jay apart?<br /><br />Me: God, no. That would require a crowbar. I’m just saying you should make <i>friends</i> with Rafe. And try to be a real friend, not a friend like you are to Chelsea. Rafe is currently the most interesting person in your life, including you.<br /><br />Violet: Was that an insult?<br /><br />Me: Do you think Rafe is psychic? <br /><br />Violet: I dunno. Does it matter? I bet if Jay was psychic he’d know I’m always right.<br /><br />Me: Yeah, okay. Call Rafe or that FBI lady next time you think about running off by yourself, okay? It might save you almost getting shot.<br /><br />Violet: Yeah, yeah, whatever. Look, I think I hear a dead body calling to me, so I’m going to run off into a deserted area by myself. Don’t tell anyone. I’m sure I’ll be fine. Later.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="566660594250443051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_441371206" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/441371206" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/441371206?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=suspense-or-thriller">suspense-or-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=beta-hero">beta-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=hybrid-multiple-genre">hybrid-multiple-genre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=reapers-necromancers-death-agents">reapers-necromancers-death-agents</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer441371206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7964401813470033874"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Romance and Murder - two great things that go together like peanut butter and chocolate.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395429i/761636.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>Okay, so maybe these two things shouldn't really go together. But it sure makes for the kind of story that I would want to read.<br/><br/><b>Three point triple six stars.</b> You do the mental math. I'm sort of freaked out to actually type the number. Yes, I am that chicken.<br/><br/>For those who aren't aware of what this series is about, it revolves around a girl named Violet who can sense dead bodies and the people who </span>
  <span id="freeText7964401813470033874" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Romance and Murder - two great things that go together like peanut butter and chocolate.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395429i/761636.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Okay, so maybe these two things shouldn't really go together. But it sure makes for the kind of story that I would want to read.<br><br><b>Three point triple six stars.</b> You do the mental math. I'm sort of freaked out to actually type the number. Yes, I am that chicken.<br><br>For those who aren't aware of what this series is about, it revolves around a girl named Violet who can sense dead bodies and the people who are responsible for those corpses by sensing echoes/imprints which connect the killer to their victim. Of course, this leaves Violet in constant danger, but she always has the support of her faithful best friend-turned love interest Jay. Creepy + romantically sweet = weird, but good mind trip. <br><br>I get why not everyone liked <i>Desires of the Dead</i> as much as <i>The Body Finder.</i> For me, both books were equally enjoyable as reads. The reason why this book was just a slight bit weaker, is because the suspense and creep factor of the first book did not even come close to the same level in book 2. In book 1, we got to spend part of the time being freaked out as we were in the mind of a serial killer. There were a couple of scenes which had me nervous in book 1. My stress level never tipped into the danger zone for this book.<br><br>However, this is not to say that <i>Desires</i> was a bad book. I might not have gotten as much of a thrill ride in the psycho killer department, but this was a fun little romp nonetheless. More of the focus was on the romance side of the spectrum, but there was at least a setup for other heavy-duty adventures in future books. We'll call this the "lovers bridge" book. In a way, the romance was better because it felt less angsty in the second installment. <br><br><b>A few random thoughts :</b><br><br>~ Using the seven deadly sins as headers when the PoV switched to the "bad" person was creative.<br>~ There's a new boy in town. While he is appealing, I'd rather not see this series go the love triangle route. Jay is one of the better male leads in YA fiction that I've read, so he deserves to keep his hero status.<br>~ The transition of the FBI into the story felt clunky and inauthentic. When you're not sure if the FBI is even legit, there's a chance that the author probably should have done a little more research.<br><br><b>Best friends-turned-romantic : a refreshing departure from the tired setup of "new and cocky guy comes to town."</b> Why can't we truly have more decent and likable guys in fiction? Is there a reason why everyone's got to be a d*ckhead? <br><br>How could you not love Jay?<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Her voice was soft. "What did you think when I first told you about the animals I found?"<br>"Violet, I was seven years old. I thought it was badass. I think I was probably even jealous."<br>She made a face at him. "Didn't you think it was creepy? Or that I was weird?"<br>"Yeah," he agreed enthusiastically. "That's why I was so jealous. I wanted to be the one finding dead bodies. You were like an animal detective or something. You were only weird 'cause you were a girl." He grinned. "But I learned to overlook that since you always took me on such cool adventures."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Granted, he is still protective, and he still has his growly moments like any guy who has a thing for a girl, but he is able to continue to be the fun best friend. We need more characters like this - people who show that life is not always about being the most chest-thumping control-freak.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Oh, and Violet," he whispered against her ear, his breath tickling her cheek, "I'm still your best friend. Don't ever forget it."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="7964401813470033874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_156254966" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156254966" />
    <a title="Kelly Marbury" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5168782-kelly-marbury"><img alt="Kelly Marbury" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443900329p2/5168782.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156254966?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly Marbury" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly Marbury" href="/user/show/5168782-kelly-marbury">Kelly Marbury</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156254966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16378447066444225738">When I first read The Body Finder I was struck with the feeling I had found something special, complete with the a great plot, heartwarming romance, suspense, and character development. So when I heard there would be a sequel I found myself counting the days until the release. Then (finally) I read Desires of the Dead and I must say I feel a little let down. <br/><br/>I stayed up all night reading The Body Finder because as much as I wanted to put it down and get some rest for work in the morning, it woul</span>
  <span id="freeText16378447066444225738" style="display:none">When I first read The Body Finder I was struck with the feeling I had found something special, complete with the a great plot, heartwarming romance, suspense, and character development. So when I heard there would be a sequel I found myself counting the days until the release. Then (finally) I read Desires of the Dead and I must say I feel a little let down. <br /><br />I stayed up all night reading The Body Finder because as much as I wanted to put it down and get some rest for work in the morning, it wouldn’t release its hold on me. Naturally, I thought that the sequel would have the same effect - but it didn’t. <br /><br />I struggled to get through this book and even found myself trying to remember why I was so enamored with the first one. To summarize my disappointments I will touch on 3 points:<br /><br />	The first being Violet. She was the biggest let down for me in this book. She was very jealous when it concerned Jay’s new-to-town friend Mike without just cause. At one point Jay even tried to make it up to Vi for spending so much time with Mike. She acted very childishly when afterwards he said he needed to stop by Mike’s to return something he’d left in the car while helping Jay with Violet’s surprise. I mean, really Violet? Get over yourself. Many other scenes in which she makes stupid mistake after stupid mistake follow this. Her inability to open up to ANYBODY throughout the book (including Jay and her family), her overreaction to a disagreement she had with Jay which caused her to miss TWO days of school and become severely depressed, her refusal to even consider her own safety as she places herself in extremely dangerous situations time after time… the list goes on and on. <br />	Second is the relationship between Violet and Jay. Though many people will wonder why I see this as a downfall because obviously Jay is head-over-heels in love with Violet and treats her as though she could do no wrong – and what could possibly be wrong with that? I see things little more realistically. The main flaws in their relationship had to do with Violet’s hang-ups. I get it. Everybody has his or her own insecurities but whereas Jay was absolutely, sickeningly PERFECT when it concerned Violet, she was the complete opposite toward him and to me the imbalance was unfair to say the least. Also, sex does not necessarily show relationship progression in a positive light. If anything, it can be the cause for more problems and confusion and in light of Violet’s lack of confidence in Jay and his feelings for her (which I outlined above) I do not feel like this helped solidify their transition from best friends to a dating relationship.<br />	Lastly, it would have been nice to get a little bit of a glimpse into the character of Rafe. As I closed the book after the final chapter, I know no more about him than when he was first introduced. I get that Derting may be trying to set things up for her next installment, but just a peek into his character would have been a nice treat. Especially since its pretty clear that if she does continue the series, he will most likely be a key player - possibly even a 2nd love interest (if all of the not-so-subtle sparks between him and Violet whenever they would touch means anything besides the fact that they both have paranormal abilities).<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16378447066444225738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_95291205" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95291205" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95291205?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=own-copy">own-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95291205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9778990830676705900">(4.5 Stars)<br/><br/><b>Desires of the Dead</b> starts off soon after the first book, and all seems to be right in the world for Violet and her best friend-turned boyfriend, Jay. That is till Violet's ability to sense the echo's of death begin to call again. This time it brings Violet to a little boy trapped in a cargo hold and soon enough the FBI start getting involved, which is only the beginning of Violets problems.<br/><br/>Written just like the first book we get the pov's in both Violet, and this time instead of the </span>
  <span id="freeText9778990830676705900" style="display:none">(4.5 Stars)<br /><br /><b>Desires of the Dead</b> starts off soon after the first book, and all seems to be right in the world for Violet and her best friend-turned boyfriend, Jay. That is till Violet's ability to sense the echo's of death begin to call again. This time it brings Violet to a little boy trapped in a cargo hold and soon enough the FBI start getting involved, which is only the beginning of Violets problems.<br /><br />Written just like the first book we get the pov's in both Violet, and this time instead of the Hunter, we have a Stalker. I actually liked this one better. The Hunters thoughts were pretty dame freaky and while the Stalker was clearly not all there, it wasn't so bad, or at least, not for me.<br /><br />Jay and Violet are hands down one of the sweetest couples in YA literature. To many yummy moments that just melted me. But, they also felt different in this one.<br />Poor Violet, she has some real hard issues to deal with and apart of me felt really bad for her, but the other part, well, it kinda wanted to smack her. Just a little.<br />In one scene she totally took it a little to far, and while I get it, I was still pretty surprised that she had that in her. The secrets she's keeping was beyond frustrating, I mean I understand that she's scared, and honestly who can blame her? But the girl has to have realized all along that she was never ever alone in this.<br />As for Jay? ~sigh~ Jay Jay Jay, what happen to ya buddy? I can almost hear the crack of the whip in the background during <i>that</i> scene. Tsk! What happened to the stead-fast, firm but gentle guy that was in the first book?<br />As always, Jay is the knight-in-shinning-armor. Fiercely protective and hopelessly devoted, and that's a good thing, but some of the scenes just...didn't add up to there original personalities, or maybe it's just me.<br />Still, I adore these two and if I'm being honest, they are the reason I love this series so much.<br /><br />On to the flip side. The Stalker. No worries, I wont spoil anything, but I will say that it's nicely done with a good twist. I didn't see it coming. I love how Derting can separate the two sides of the story. It's very complex and intense and definitely kept me on my toes. As for the new characters, they were fine I guess, I don't really have anything to say about them. The FBI was interesting, I can see something happening (hopefully) in the next book.<br /><br />Overall, I really loved this one. Sure it had a few scenes that upset me, but that's why I loved it. If a book can piss me off then it means I care, or well, most of the time anywho's. This has all the elements I love in a great book. Mystery, suspense and swoon-worthy characters. I hope the series keeps going, I'm not ready for it to end just yet.<br /><br />Thanks Alexa for sending me a copy! Loved it!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9778990830676705900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_190162339" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190162339" />
    <a title="Asenath" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1293092-asenath"><img alt="Asenath" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1253382851p2/1293092.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/190162339?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Asenath" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Asenath" href="/user/show/1293092-asenath">Asenath</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1293092-asenath?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1293092-asenath?shelf=wishlist">wishlist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1293092-asenath?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190162339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3568047581877510334">What. The. Heck. This book was SOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO disappointing! I loved <i>The Body Finder</i>, so I was really looking forward to this one. <i>The Body Finder</i> had an excellent plot, good characterization, awesome twists and was so suspenseful that I literally could not put it down. But this one was hard for me to finish.<br/><br/>Things I liked:<br/>-The plot wasn't exactly the same as the first book, and could have been good.<br/>-The addition of Sara and Rafe. I want to learn more about Rafe, and would be interested in </span>
  <span id="freeText3568047581877510334" style="display:none">What. The. Heck. This book was SOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO disappointing! I loved <i>The Body Finder</i>, so I was really looking forward to this one. <i>The Body Finder</i> had an excellent plot, good characterization, awesome twists and was so suspenseful that I literally could not put it down. But this one was hard for me to finish.<br /><br />Things I liked:<br />-The plot wasn't exactly the same as the first book, and could have been good.<br />-The addition of Sara and Rafe. I want to learn more about Rafe, and would be interested in learning his story<br /><br />Things I wish had been changed:<br /><br />-About 100 pages should have been cut from this book. Most of it was Violet whining, or being unsure, or "deeply" kissing Jay. Boring.<br /><br />-Violet was super annoying in this book. I remember being frustrated with her sometimes in The Body Finder, but her stupidity has no limits in this book. WHY DO YOU KEEP GOING OFF BY YOURSELF VIOLET? WHY?!? You claim you don't want to upset your family, that you want to protect them but EVERY TIME you go out on your own you come back an emotional/literal wreck and then refuse to tell them what's going on, because you don't want to worry them. Guess what, they're already worried! And her reasons for not trusting people are stupid, and oh so contrived.<br /><br />-Contrived, contrived, contrived. This plot was predictable. There were no twists. Well, I guess there was one, but it was contrived, and therefores super easy to figure out. In fact, I figured out everything about half of the way through. I was hoping I'd be wrong....but I wasn't.<br /><br />-A completely unnecessary sex scene. While it wasn't graphic/explicit, it was still unnecessary. I've said this many times, and I will continue to say it: when a girl has sex at such a young age [yes, 16 is young. I know you think you are super mature, but you're not, sorry] there are lasting psychological repercussions. Sure, the guy can be a real gem, but USUALLY he is not. Girls are *already* far too willing to believe that the guy they are dating is the exception to every rule, that he loves them, will never leave them, etc, when REALLY, the guy just wants to get it on. Teenage girl readers should not feel like this is the acceptable norm. I know that teenagers are capable of making their own decisions and won't do something JUST because they read about it, but if you're going to have your characters have sex, be realistic about it. If she broke up with her boyfriend THE NIGHT AFTER having sex, there would be A LOT of psychological damage done.<br /><br />I think that's all. So disappointing. I don't know if I'll read the 3rd book in the series...</span>
  <a data-text-id="3568047581877510334" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_174370099" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/174370099" />
    <a title="Paradoxical" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1964421-paradoxical"><img alt="Paradoxical" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349572735p2/1964421.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/174370099?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paradoxical" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paradoxical" href="/user/show/1964421-paradoxical">Paradoxical</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1964421-paradoxical?shelf=2011-reading-list">2011-reading-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1964421-paradoxical?shelf=books-otherwise">books-otherwise</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174370099" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3361421459856336162">Argh. It was like in the span between the first book and this one, Violet has gotten ten times more melodramatic. It's so irritating seeing a character backslide like that. She's jealous of the time Jay is spending without her, she doesn't talk to her family or Jay about her problems (even though they have known for <i>years</i> about her ability to sense the dead), and I spend a good portion of the time wanting to slap some more sense into her. It was like the author took her main character and forced</span>
  <span id="freeText3361421459856336162" style="display:none">Argh. It was like in the span between the first book and this one, Violet has gotten ten times more melodramatic. It's so irritating seeing a character backslide like that. She's jealous of the time Jay is spending without her, she doesn't talk to her family or Jay about her problems (even though they have known for <i>years</i> about her ability to sense the dead), and I spend a good portion of the time wanting to slap some more sense into her. It was like the author took her main character and forced emotional upheaval all over her just to give the book more drama. <br /><br />Then there's Violet's friend, Chelsea, who is an awful person. I don't care if she seems cool, or that she speaks her mind, there are ways to do that without being a jerk. Every time she wanders across the page I lose most of my interest and just wait until she goes away. How Chelsea is any better than the cheerleaders that the main character derides is beyond my understanding.<br /><br />And, oh jeez, Violet's inability to stand up for herself, to tell her family and Jay what is going on, is the most frustrating part of the book. Someone connected to the FBI starts snooping around and what does she do? <i>Not</i> tell her family. She spends so much time trying to run away from reality that I can hardly stand her now. Jay is perfectly sweet to her (to an almost sickening degree, honestly), and she doesn't nearly match him in that. I liked them together in the first book, but in the second I was mostly feeling sorry that Jay even stuck around Violet.<br /><br />The plot was shallow and seemed mostly... petty. Then there was the reveal at the end that sort of just pops up and I didn't care at all. I expected a lot more from the book--the least that the book was be all right like the first--only to have those expectations fall flat. 1-2 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3361421459856336162" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_106388311" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/106388311" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/106388311?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=zzread-august-2011">zzread-august-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=library-finds">library-finds</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106388311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9210171579559055471">2.5 - 3 stars <br/><br/>Desires of the Dead is the second book in Kimberly Derting’s Body Finder series. The premise of this series is quite original. The main character Violet has a special ability: She can hear, smell, or see echoes of the dead. The dead – both human and animals – call to her. A matching echo can be found on the murderer. Oftentimes Violet will find dead animals, but there have been occasions where she finds human remains.<br/><br/>This book takes place three months after the events of the first </span>
  <span id="freeText9210171579559055471" style="display:none">2.5 - 3 stars <br /><br />Desires of the Dead is the second book in Kimberly Derting’s Body Finder series. The premise of this series is quite original. The main character Violet has a special ability: She can hear, smell, or see echoes of the dead. The dead – both human and animals – call to her. A matching echo can be found on the murderer. Oftentimes Violet will find dead animals, but there have been occasions where she finds human remains.<br /><br />This book takes place three months after the events of the first book. I will preface this review to say that I really enjoyed the first book and while it had a few niggling problems, I gave that book 5 stars or an A rating. This book did not strike me in the same way. Those few niggling things that bothered me in the first book drove me nuts in this one. <br /><br />First the good – the story is well written and it has a nice element of suspense. I liked how the author interspersed regular chapters with chapters from the mind of a troubled young girl. It was a little too easy to guess who it was and not as creepy as the first book. <br /><br />Despite my rant below, I did like most of the characters, especially Jay, the most “awesomest” boyfriend ever. Jay is loyal, protective, loving, and romantic. A 16 year old boy who creates romantic picnics lit by glow sticks? Jay is just too good to be true. Jay and Violet have been best friends for a long time. Jay understands Violet’s talent and how it affects her. <br /><br />So we have a girl who can find dead people. Not a particularly safe past time for a young teenage girl. So herein lays my problem with this book. The main character does way too many things with no regard for her personal safety. Violet drives to Seattle in the middle of the night to check out a container at a pier because she felt the call of a body. Port? Pier? Container? Not the safest place to be on your own at the best of times.<br /><br />Other stuff happens to Violet and again her disregard for her personal safety bothered me. Someone leaves a dead cat next to her car. A threatening note is left on her windshield. Crank phone calls. Does she report any of this? No. Here’s the kicker – her uncle is the police chief, but she doesn’t want to tell him because she is afraid that her parents would worry. <br /><br />Violet’s lack of communication was another issue for me. Rather than talking over her problems with her someone, or anyone, she just shut down. This led to many misunderstandings. She is also jealous when her boyfriend makes friends with Mike, the new student. <br /><br />I was struck by the lack of parental presence in this book. Violet does not go to them for help, nor do they act like parents. They don’t seem too concerned she was out late; they only worry about her feelings. This is a girl who just 3 months earlier had her life threatened. Why would they not be concerned about her safety and well being? <br /><br />All criticism aside, I really did enjoy this book and I will be reading the next book when it comes out. <br /><br /><b>Check out my review at <a href="http://badassbookreviews.com/2011/08/09/review-desires-of-the-dead-by-kimberly-derting/" rel="nofollow noopener">Badass Book Reviews</a></b><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9210171579559055471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=series-abandoned">series-abandoned</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15600350472863458542">2.5 stars. Desires of the Dead was not nearly as good as The Body Finder. I thought The Body Finder was a great stand-alone book and I sort of wished it had stayed that way <br/><br/>There were a couple of edge of your seat moments in this one, but most of the time I felt like Violet was an idiot. She suddenly feels as though she can't talk to anyone and starts hiding everything, and the reasoning behind it is just flimsy to me. Where was the confident Violet? She seemed like a different person in this bo</span>
  <span id="freeText15600350472863458542" style="display:none">2.5 stars. Desires of the Dead was not nearly as good as The Body Finder. I thought The Body Finder was a great stand-alone book and I sort of wished it had stayed that way <br /><br />There were a couple of edge of your seat moments in this one, but most of the time I felt like Violet was an idiot. She suddenly feels as though she can't talk to anyone and starts hiding everything, and the reasoning behind it is just flimsy to me. Where was the confident Violet? She seemed like a different person in this book.<br /><br />I thought the romance between Violet and Jay in the Body Finder was sweet, the way they realized that they felt more than just friendship for each other. However, in this book we are assaulted with their hormones. Jay is trying to hold off on having sex, but Violet keeps pressuring him into it. This went on for half of the book until they finally give in and have sex, which was not surprising considering the situations they kept putting themselves in. <br /><br />I have real issues with 16 year olds having sex. Violet is already conflicted and confused about the change in their relationship and having sex is only something that will complicate it more. She is just so immature in this book. And to prove my point, she completely over reacts when Jay doesn't believe something that she does, and thinks that their whole relationship is over because of it. She goes all to pieces and can't handle going to school or anything. She holes up in her room for two days! I mean really if she can't handle this tiny little bump in a relationship, then there is no way she needs to be in a sexual relationship. <br /><br />Overall I felt the book was pretty predictable. There was no real mystery about who did anything, except for who killed the little boy at the beginning of the book, and that was because the book wasn't about that murder. It was just thrown in there to introduce Violet to the Profiler who she obviously will be working with from now on in the rest of the series. I also could have done without the language near the end of the book. Why throw in the "f" word several times suddenly? <br /><br />Overall I was disappointed in this book and have decided not to continue on with this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15600350472863458542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11254090111267370918">Holy cow! Desires of the Dead is one of the best sequels I've read in a really long time. I forgot how amazing Kimberly's writing is. I'm literally at a lost for words. <br/><br/>Wow. Just...wow!<br/><br/>What I love about Desires of the Dead is how Kimberly write's from Violet's point of view, but switches every now and then to "the bad guy's" POV. This is what originally hooked me on The Body Finder. It's dark, it's twisted, it's made of win!<br/><br/>Violet and Jay's relationship begins to develope into something hotter, </span>
  <span id="freeText11254090111267370918" style="display:none">Holy cow! Desires of the Dead is one of the best sequels I've read in a really long time. I forgot how amazing Kimberly's writing is. I'm literally at a lost for words. <br /><br />Wow. Just...wow!<br /><br />What I love about Desires of the Dead is how Kimberly write's from Violet's point of view, but switches every now and then to "the bad guy's" POV. This is what originally hooked me on The Body Finder. It's dark, it's twisted, it's made of win!<br /><br />Violet and Jay's relationship begins to develope into something hotter, sexier and more complicated than it was in The Body Finder. Just like all couples, they start dealing with intimacy and trust issues. It's not always happy, but at least it's interesting!<br /><br />Unlike a lot of sequels out there, this one comes full circle. I really enjoyed that. Sometimes, too much of a cliffhanger can become not only tiresome, but irritating. In this case, it's just the right amount of satisfaction and craving for more.<br /> <br />Fans of The Body Finder will jump and cheer for Desires of the Dead. It's deliciously dangerous in all the right ways.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15358164276279396479"><br/>Well, I'm on a roll. This is the third book in a row that I have read this week in a matter of days. I'm very pleased by this. Completely.<br/><br/><br/>To that end, I read Desires of the Dead by Kimberly Derting. This is the sequel to this year's The Body Finder. Wow. Derting does it again. These books make me so happy, and desperate for a sequel. Which means I now have to wait until Spring(ish?) 2012. Whinge!!!<br/><br/>Anywho, intelligent review. Yes! Yes, I can do that.<br/><br/>Violet and Jay have developed their romance. As</span>
  <span id="freeText15358164276279396479" style="display:none"><br />Well, I'm on a roll. This is the third book in a row that I have read this week in a matter of days. I'm very pleased by this. Completely.<br /><br /><br />To that end, I read Desires of the Dead by Kimberly Derting. This is the sequel to this year's The Body Finder. Wow. Derting does it again. These books make me so happy, and desperate for a sequel. Which means I now have to wait until Spring(ish?) 2012. Whinge!!!<br /><br />Anywho, intelligent review. Yes! Yes, I can do that.<br /><br />Violet and Jay have developed their romance. As they get deeper Violet becomes aware of new, protective feelings of Jay. She's become territorial, particularly when a new brother and sister, Mike and Megan, move into town. Besides that, Violet keeps experiences echos that signify bodies, bodies that will eat at her until she sees them laid to rest. She's already dealt with a mass murderer but now she has a new conflict - someone is stalking her, and Violet has to find out why... and who.<br /><br />Like I said, or rather implied, I love these books. They are creepy in all the right ways, tender in all the right moments and, better yet, have a wholly believable female character helming the ship. Violet is perfect, her voice rings. It's refreshing to see a heroine who doesn't just crumble under her romance with Mr. Perfect (coughcoughbellacoughcough). Violet is independent, headstrong, intelligent, and charismatic. Violet also swears, and does stupid things, and gets horny, and jumps to conclusions. Violet is a real character, which makes her that much more fun to read. It's wonderful to find something in the young adult genre that is not just another abysmal Twilight clone. Especially now that so many publishers are publishing abysmal Twilight clones. I realize I am more or less repeating my impressions of The Body Finder, but the point is even more extraordinary with a sequel... the sequel stands up to the first one. That's probably the best praise I can offer to Derting.<br /><br />5 out of 5 stars. If you haven't read The Body Finder yet, you must.<br /><br />- review courtesy of <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bibliopunkkreads.com">www.bibliopunkkreads.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15358164276279396479" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_144580285" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144580285" />
    <a title="Milly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4000502-milly"><img alt="Milly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291008553p2/4000502.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144580285?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Milly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Milly" href="/user/show/4000502-milly">Milly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4000502-milly?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4000502-milly?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4000502-milly?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144580285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11789764113917722954">*ARC Review (amazing enough, I didn't find any typos)<br/><br/>I have always admired Kimberly Derting's writing. Body Finder was beautifully written and the beginnings of Desires of the Dead was just as beautiful. The setting of the book takes place again in a small town in Washington but the book starts off in Seattle when Violet takes a trip with her friend. The way Derting described Seattle deliciously beautiful makes me miss Seattle and reminisce of my vacation trip one summer. Starting out Desires of</span>
  <span id="freeText11789764113917722954" style="display:none">*ARC Review (amazing enough, I didn't find any typos)<br /><br />I have always admired Kimberly Derting's writing. Body Finder was beautifully written and the beginnings of Desires of the Dead was just as beautiful. The setting of the book takes place again in a small town in Washington but the book starts off in Seattle when Violet takes a trip with her friend. The way Derting described Seattle deliciously beautiful makes me miss Seattle and reminisce of my vacation trip one summer. Starting out Desires of the Dead with this beautiful prose definitely had me entranced from the very start. <br /><br />In this second installment, we see a development in Violet's ability to sense the dead. In addition to being able to see colors, hear distinct sounds and smell particular odors that come with each dead spirit, the dead could now somehow visit her dreams as well. As she finds another dead body in a container in Seattle, somehow the FBI finds her in their radar and attempt to recruit her to help them solve some cold cases involving missing persons. It is in this process that she meets another teenager with unique abilities just like her. Enters Rafe and his strange ability that eventually saves Violet in the end. Rafe is very mysterious and has a potential to be another significant character in this series. Although I find him interesting, I sure don't want him interfering in Violet and Jay's relationship in the future. I hope Derting doesn't make him a third wheel in the next installment. <br /><br />Although I enjoyed this book very much, I have just two qualms about the book. First, I didn't find Meg's part in this book believable as an obvious villain. Her role in it just seemed too convenient and I find her character as an accessory and inconsequential. I am sure that Derting penned her character in as a main distraction to deter us from finding the true villain in the book and to bring in the mystery and thriller that surrounds the true killer. What I didn't find believable enough is Meg's actions involving the cat (especially if she cared about that cat that much) and her stalking ways. I get that she's troubled over the loss of her mother, the downward spiral of her father, and the unrequited feelings she has for Jay...but...to result to these behaviors? Derting just failed to convince me here. Again, this is my personal opinion and I could be completely wrong about it. But, it was a part of this book that bothered me. <br /><br />Secondly, Violet oh Violet. Her characterization as a whiny and insecure person in this installment annoyed me. It made me wonder again how someone like Jay could like someone like her. She was a rain cloud hanging over him constantly. I loved Jay's character the more as I liked Violet's character the less. It annoyed me that Violet's character was portrayed as being weak and so dependent on Jay. Come on Violet, Jay needs to have some guy time with his friends too. He can't spend every waking time just with you! How could you be jealous of another guy?! Jay's apparently the only mature teenager in this book and I loved his character for it. <br /><br />One of the reasons I liked about this book was Jay. If there was a male literary character I wanted animated, it would be Jay for sure! His patience for Violet and his unfailing loyalty to her is so admirable! He's even more attractive because he doesn't know how good-looking he is. And, he truly is a nice guy through and through. Violet just doesn't deserve him, at least in this book, unless she grows up! Sorry Violet. I just find you a little disheartening in this book. <br /><br />But, like I said, I still enjoyed reading this book and I would definitely look forward to the third in the series. I still recommend you pick this up especially if you're a fan of Derting's writing and of the series. I just thought Body Finder was a lot better than this one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11789764113917722954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_802823204" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/802823204" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/802823204?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=my-favorite-covers">my-favorite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer802823204" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8406854335567856579">So here I am again with a short and sweet review. Violet and Jay are only continuing their journey from book one, and there's no need to write a long, drawn out review about their undying love for one another and Violet's ability to 'sense' the unsettled dead that call to her. <br/><br/>More than anything, this book was based around the growth of Jay and Violet's relationship-the trust that is earned and given between a new couple. But Jay and Violet have been best friends since they were young, so the tr</span>
  <span id="freeText8406854335567856579" style="display:none">So here I am again with a short and sweet review. Violet and Jay are only continuing their journey from book one, and there's no need to write a long, drawn out review about their undying love for one another and Violet's ability to 'sense' the unsettled dead that call to her. <br><br>More than anything, this book was based around the growth of Jay and Violet's relationship-the trust that is earned and given between a new couple. But Jay and Violet have been best friends since they were young, so the trust is already there in spades...until she has to tell Jay what she believes about his new friend's family, causing a rift among them they've never experienced before.<br><br>I loved how the 'killer's' POV was represented in this story-through the seven deadly sins. I thought it was cool how she began the incorporation of the sins into the mind of the weirdo that was supposedly stalking Violet. It did become a little forced and a bit of a stretch when the sins started to dwindle down to <i>gluttony</i> and <i>sloth</i>, but I still liked what came of the story because of this creativity. I do wish the author chose to keep the identity somewhat mysterious for us to figure out as readers in each installment of this series, but the story is still good enough to keep me interested without the mystery. Even with the 'twists' she generally throws in, they aren't hard to figure out. But, as I said, I still thoroughly enjoyed the story despite the lack of unpredictability. <br><br>There's still a somewhat corny feel to the story, but I think it was less so in this second one. I am used to the writing and it's so subtle that I can hardly complain about it-I've chosen to continue the series so why not enjoy the light, fun read? I still love Jay and Vi, they make an adorable couple despite their little fight that ultimately tested how strongly they felt for one another, and I am excited to finish this series with books three and four on a strong note.<br><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews visit<br><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img height="240" width="385" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407869528i/10772466._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> </i></span>

<div id="review_98023985" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98023985" />
    <a title="Alexa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1894085-alexa"><img alt="Alexa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393730599p2/1894085.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98023985?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexa" href="/user/show/1894085-alexa">Alexa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=2010-reads">2010-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=gave-away">gave-away</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98023985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17731532837571448440"><br/>My review can also be found on my blog <a href='http://collections-books.blogspot.com/2011/01/review-desires-of-dead-by-kimberly.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Collections</a>.<br/><br/><i>Desires of the Dead</i> starts off a few months after <i>The Body Finder</i>. Everything seems to have pretty much returned to normal for Violet after the incident during the Homecoming dance. Things change, though, when she discovers the body of a young boy stashed in a cargo ship container in Seattle. Violet is later contacted by the FBI, who want to know <i>exactly</i> how she managed to locate the body. This is when Violet's problems begin.<br/><br/>It's hard not to co</span>
  <span id="freeText17731532837571448440" style="display:none"><br />My review can also be found on my blog <a href="http://collections-books.blogspot.com/2011/01/review-desires-of-dead-by-kimberly.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Collections</a>.<br /><br /><i>Desires of the Dead</i> starts off a few months after <i>The Body Finder</i>. Everything seems to have pretty much returned to normal for Violet after the incident during the Homecoming dance. Things change, though, when she discovers the body of a young boy stashed in a cargo ship container in Seattle. Violet is later contacted by the FBI, who want to know <i>exactly</i> how she managed to locate the body. This is when Violet's problems begin.<br /><br />It's hard not to compare this book with <i>The Body Finder</i>. Both books are similar in that there's chapters for the 'stalker' and Violet needs to figure out that person's identity before an innocent person gets hurt or even killed. Some of the differences in this book are that there's a couple new characters and Violet is much more secretive. I will admit that those are the reasons I didn't love it like I did the previous book. Of course new characters are to be expected, but I didn't have much of a feel for them. The brother and sister felt random. And the FBI characters seemed really important, but they didn't get much scenes. (Maybe the author is saving them for a third book?) As for Violet and her secrets, I got pretty annoyed with her when she kept information from everyone, including Jay. Those secrets just led to more problems and caused her to be upset throughout the book. Sometimes it was a bit too much.<br /><br />There were some other issues I had with the book, but they were minor compared to how I felt about the new characters and the secrets. And while I didn't love it as much as <i>The Body Finder</i>, I did enjoy <i>Desires of the Dead</i> overall. The moments between Violet and Jay were probably my favorite parts to read. I would recommend this sequel to those who liked <i>The Body Finder</i> and want to know what happens next with Violet <s>(and Jay)</s>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17731532837571448440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_149976276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/149976276" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3771487-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366667114p2/3771487.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/149976276?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/3771487-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer149976276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1404096807458136029">I am having a hard time writing a review for this novel. It was every bit as good as The Bodyfinder. All the same characters were there, but the focus was more on the kids this time than the parents. Chelsea had more "face time" so we got to learn more about her. Jay and Violet's relationship continued with some major hiccups. I'd say Jay showed some character growth, showing some more vulnerability where it comes to Violet, and maturity at not forcing things out of her before she's ready to tal</span>
  <span id="freeText1404096807458136029" style="display:none">I am having a hard time writing a review for this novel. It was every bit as good as The Bodyfinder. All the same characters were there, but the focus was more on the kids this time than the parents. Chelsea had more "face time" so we got to learn more about her. Jay and Violet's relationship continued with some major hiccups. I'd say Jay showed some character growth, showing some more vulnerability where it comes to Violet, and maturity at not forcing things out of her before she's ready to talk. But I felt like Violet took two steps back. She was childish, not telling Jay when she got threats, when she felt the echos calling to her. When she had suspicions. She lied by omission quite a bit saying she was protecting her family. And all the time she was putting herself in danger. I didn't like who she was in this novel. Instead of being strong, she was stupid and childish, very immature. I hope she grows up in the next book.<br /><br />The plot line moved at a fast pace again, barely letting you catch your breath. Just when I thought it was going one way, it went another and then a curve ball was thrown in and I thought "Hmm, maybe." I turned out to be wrong, but who knows in a later book. The suspense was there, the terror, the mystery all there.<br /><br />The romance was there, too. It was so good I read late in the night and picked it up first thing the next day. I love Kimberly Derting's style. It's sharp and lean. Not too much description, just enough to let you get a mental image. The dialogue is great, especially Chelsea. She's snarky and funny. I really loved this book.<br /><br />I guess my only disappointment was Violet's increasing stupidity as the novel went on. Everything else was great. I do like where the story line seems to be headed, I just hope the dreaded triangle isn't going to come into play. Please.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />This is a book for older teens as sex is an issue in this book. Along with death.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1404096807458136029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2315369624" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2315369624" />
    <a title="Jacquelyn Simon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5223246-jacquelyn-simon"><img alt="Jacquelyn Simon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598812176p2/5223246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2315369624?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacquelyn Simon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacquelyn Simon" href="/user/show/5223246-jacquelyn-simon">Jacquelyn Simon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2315369624&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2315369624" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11378438013859641251">So up until 148 pages into the book, I thought this was going to be my review. This book is feeling really similar to The Naturals by Jennifer Lynn Barnes. The Naturals is one of my all time favorite series, but it’s to the point that I’m getting bored with this particular book. I originally really enjoyed The Body Finder, because the concept was so unique. Now, the sequel, just feels unoriginal. I guess I just feel disappointed of its lack of originality, or perhaps, in the world of mystery boo</span>
  <span id="freeText11378438013859641251" style="display:none">So up until 148 pages into the book, I thought this was going to be my review. This book is feeling really similar to The Naturals by Jennifer Lynn Barnes. The Naturals is one of my all time favorite series, but it’s to the point that I’m getting bored with this particular book. I originally really enjoyed The Body Finder, because the concept was so unique. Now, the sequel, just feels unoriginal. I guess I just feel disappointed of its lack of originality, or perhaps, in the world of mystery books, I’ve read all there is to read in the genre. I certainly hope, it’s NOT the latter.<br /><br />Since finishing the book, I realized that it’s not fair to compare it to The Naturals, because, nothing really happened in this book. That’s my main criticism. Sure, there were a few times something somewhat interesting happened, but most of the time it was just Violet being moody. If you market a book to be about a teenager who finds dead bodies, I would certainly hope it would be more fast paced and less of a romance than this book. I love a good romance, but this book mainly consisted of the love life of two sixteen year olds. If I wanted to read an entire book like that, I would’ve picked up a contemporary, not a mystery.<br />My last complaint has to do with both books, which is that they tied up too neatly. I hate it when I read a mystery series and all of the plot lines get tied up in a nice little bow and everyone lives happily ever after. Like, I’m sorry, but life doesn’t happen like that so it just bugs me when authors choose those endings. It feels like a cop out and honestly endings like that are too boring and innocent for me. The first book could’ve honestly been a standalone. This book was not needed.</span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lincy Cybelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lincy Cybelle" href="/user/show/3158399-lincy-cybelle">Lincy Cybelle</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer150640521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5960680609475899480">I hate to say it, but I was frustrated with this second Body Finder story. Not because Kim Derting isn't a fine writer. Wow, she is. I love her style, and will definitely read the next book despite being out of sorts with this one. But Violet, the heroine, frustrated me so much in DooD that I found myself putting it down now and then and reading other things. Unfortunately, I felt Violet committed that heroine sin of acting TSTL a few times too often, being unwilling to let anyone know when she </span>
  <span id="freeText5960680609475899480" style="display:none">I hate to say it, but I was frustrated with this second Body Finder story. Not because Kim Derting isn't a fine writer. Wow, she is. I love her style, and will definitely read the next book despite being out of sorts with this one. But Violet, the heroine, frustrated me so much in DooD that I found myself putting it down now and then and reading other things. Unfortunately, I felt Violet committed that heroine sin of acting TSTL a few times too often, being unwilling to let anyone know when she went out alone...at night...in deserted places... and when she was stalked, and when authorities contacted her...it just made no sense to me after all she went through in the previous book, despite the natural instinct of her character to keep her ability to herself. I felt she'd learned nothing and hadn't evolved credibly. <br /><br />That said...I still love Kim's story telling, there's something about her atmospheric style that grabs me and I enjoy, despite wanting to off Violet myself a time or two. I am looking forward to whatever happens next. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5960680609475899480" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14916487680644276881">The second book in the Body Finder series. Again another great read from Derting, although I didn't quite love it as much as the first book. It took me a bit longer to get into it but once I did I was hooked. The plot is intriguing and I love the way that Derting is setting up this series adding in some new elements. It certainly has got me excited for the next book. Jay and Violet were gorgeous as usual. I LOVE their romance. Sweet yet full of passion and heart. Definitely worth a read!<br/></span>
