<div id="review_341718141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/341718141" />
    <a title="nick (the infinite limits of love)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2993271-nick-the-infinite-limits-of-love"><img alt="nick (the infinite limits of love)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606193187p2/2993271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/341718141?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="nick (the infinite limits of love)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="nick (the infinite limits of love)" href="/user/show/2993271-nick-the-infinite-limits-of-love">nick (the infinite limits of love)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer341718141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7547816376123005032"><br/><b>Read more of my reviews at <a href='http://nicksbookblog93.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nick's Book Blog</a></b><br/><br/>I read The Body Finder some time back and I enjoyed the book. Because of that, I was very excited to jump into the second book, Desires Of The Dead. However, I felt like the book didn't really satisfy as a sequel and I ended up being disappointed.<br/><br/>Violet is still recovering from the murder cases that she dealt with last year when she comes across yet another body of a young boy who was kidnapped some time back. In doing so, she attracts the attention of </span>
  <span id="freeText7547816376123005032" style="display:none"><br /><b>Read more of my reviews at <a href="http://nicksbookblog93.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Nick's Book Blog</a></b><br /><br />I read The Body Finder some time back and I enjoyed the book. Because of that, I was very excited to jump into the second book, Desires Of The Dead. However, I felt like the book didn't really satisfy as a sequel and I ended up being disappointed.<br /><br />Violet is still recovering from the murder cases that she dealt with last year when she comes across yet another body of a young boy who was kidnapped some time back. In doing so, she attracts the attention of the FBI. At the same time, someone keeps sending Violet threatening messages.<br /><br />When I read a sequel, I expect a main character to have grown emotionally from the previous book. Violet, in my opinion, went downhill instead of going uphill. She acted incredibly stupid and took rash and hasty decisions that made her seem immature. You would have thought that with everything she had gone through in the previous book, she wouldn't ever go out alone in search of dead bodies, but no, Violet constantly kept going out in the middle of the night. I was incredibly frustrated by her behavior. On top of that, she never talked about the bodies that she found with members of her family or her boyfriend, all of whom knew about her secret abilities. These very people were a constant support and help to her in the previous book and it's unfathomable why she refused to share her discoveries with them. Even when it came to Jay, she acted hypocritical and childish. She clearly didn't trust him with her secrets, but when she confessed to him about the possible identity of her stalker, he had a tough time believing it and he told her that. What did our dear Violet do ? She threw a fit about how Jay did not trust her and broke up with him ! I was like "Really, Violet ?" People in relationships have disagreements, but does that mean you break up with them when you have differing opinions ?<br /><br />The romance in The Body Finder was really cute. In Desires Of The Dead, it became downright sappy and completely annoying. All Violet and Jay did was making out on every occasion. Like I mentioned above, Violet had huge trust issues when it came to Jay. I couldn't understand why. He was a good guy and he was her best friend for such a long time. Because of that, their relationship seemed unrealistic. A relationship isn't only about kisses and dates, it's also about trust. It, also, annoyed me how Violet became jealous of Jay's new friend, Michael. She kept saying that she had to compete for Jay's affection now. Seriously, did she expect him to be constantly around her ? Hypocritical, considering the fact that she refused to share her secrets with him. Plus, I thought Jay was a little too overprotective of Violet. There was basically no chemistry between the characters and overall, it was a let-down.<br /><br />I even found the plot line to be bland this time around. It was very predictable and I had already guessed the guilty party early on. One aspect that I love when I read murder/mystery books, is the actual element of suspense. Desires Of The Dead failed in that department. While the previous book was highly entertaining, this one ended up being a bore. There was nothing really captivating about the whole story. The fact that Violet's parents were so absent throughout the book was also very concerning. I didn't understand how they weren't aware that their daughter often wandered about late at night. One other thing that bugged me was the whole thing with the FBI. Correct me if I'm wrong, but isn't the FBI supposed to obtain permission from the parents before they can question a minor ? This book had my eyes rolling continuously throughout my reading !<br /><br />I expected something more epic from Desires Of The Dead. I wanted it to be more exciting and enthralling than it was. Unfortunately, this book just wasn't for me. I will give the third book a shot since I already purchased my copy, but I don't have high hopes. If Violet keeps acting immature in that one, it might end up being a DNF for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7547816376123005032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_183253157" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183253157" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3947264-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389401312p2/3947264.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/183253157?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/3947264-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of The Body Finder</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=big-romance">big-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=love-geometry">love-geometry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=multiple-narrators">multiple-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=no-sleep-tonight">no-sleep-tonight</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183253157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9723729096895938806">2.5 stars.<br/><br/>So, just to be clear, I gave this 2 (and a half) stars in true Goodreads fashion-- it's not that I didn't like it; I thought it was okay. I definitely enjoyed it more than its predecessor, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6261522.The_Body_Finder__The_Body_Finder___1_' title='The Body Finder (The Body Finder, #1) by Kimberly Derting' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Body Finder</a>. For one thing, Jay's kisses were only described as "possessive" once or twice. A step in the right direction!<br/><br/>I truly don't have much to say about this book. It was a decent way to pass the hours. It alternated between bland and engrossing. It may have been one of the most predictable</span>
  <span id="freeText9723729096895938806" style="display:none">2.5 stars.<br /><br />So, just to be clear, I gave this 2 (and a half) stars in true Goodreads fashion-- it's not that I didn't like it; I thought it was okay. I definitely enjoyed it more than its predecessor, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6261522.The_Body_Finder__The_Body_Finder___1_" title="The Body Finder (The Body Finder, #1) by Kimberly Derting" rel="nofollow noopener">The Body Finder</a>. For one thing, Jay's kisses were only described as "possessive" once or twice. A step in the right direction!<br /><br />I truly don't have much to say about this book. It was a decent way to pass the hours. It alternated between bland and engrossing. It may have been one of the most predictable books I've ever read, at least for a book that's real appeal is in the "mystery" of the plot. But somehow I didn't get too annoyed. There was something comforting, at times even <i>beautiful</i>, about watching the story unfold just as I had expected. I think it could have been much less predictable if the prologue had been written differently-- as it is, it reveals too much. <br /><br />A big, fat compliment I can give this book is that Violet, the main character, didn't make me want to scream. Meaning, despite the fact that I always figured out stuff before she did, it normally only took her a few extra pages to catch up with me. And even when I had the big picture of it all clear in my mind, I couldn't fault her for not getting it, because it made sense for her to not put the pieces together as easily as I, an objective observer, could. <br /><br />The beginning of the book was really bad, though. The writing style is so painfully mediocre that I didn't even want to turn the pages. But as the book progresses, my tolerance level increased and the plot picked up, so it was easy to get past it. That's not to say that the writing drastically improved (even as I was mildly enjoying the book, I still cringed). I don't think the author is good at the whole telling vs. showing thing, or at dialogue. But there were moments where I thought the writing was verging on good, usually involving scenery. <br /><br />And bonus points for handling sex in a thoughtful and responsible (if not quite emotionally deep) manner! Woo hooo.<br /><br />P.S. I liked the plot about Violet venturing to share her secret with others. I felt hilariously defensive of the secret right along with her at first, but as the book went on I learned to see the good in confiding it. I'm moderately looking forward to the sequel to see who else she shares it with and what exactly Rafe's power is.<br /><br />P.P.S. I don't care what anybody says, Chelsea is hilarious. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9723729096895938806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_122507073" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122507073" />
    <a title="Debbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1945325-debbie"><img alt="Debbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301006382p2/1945325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122507073?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie" href="/user/show/1945325-debbie">Debbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1945325-debbie?shelf=flowers">flowers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1945325-debbie?shelf=pink">pink</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122507073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18031128244314303374">If you read my review of The Body Finder then you know I loved that and was so excited when I was able to get my hands on the second book in this series. While you are pretty much able to predict what happens in this sequel it was still a wonderful book that I could not put down. Violet is pulled into another mystery as she tries to figure out who is stalking her and leaving her ominous messages while also trying to adjust to going from best friends with Jay to boyfriend/girlfriend with him. <br/><br/>The</span>
  <span id="freeText18031128244314303374" style="display:none">If you read my review of The Body Finder then you know I loved that and was so excited when I was able to get my hands on the second book in this series. While you are pretty much able to predict what happens in this sequel it was still a wonderful book that I could not put down. Violet is pulled into another mystery as she tries to figure out who is stalking her and leaving her ominous messages while also trying to adjust to going from best friends with Jay to boyfriend/girlfriend with him. <br /><br />The Characters<br /><br />I still love Jay but Ms. Derting introduces a new mystery guy, Rafe, who I was anxiously waiting to learn more about through out the entire book. He's good looking, mysterious and apparently has powers of his own. What those powers are is a mystery waiting to be unraveled.<br /><br />Jay is still Mr. Dependable and it is cute how much he worships Violet's uncle after having his life saved by him.<br /><br />Violet still continues to make some dumb decisions that made me shake my head but I suppose that just sets her up nicely to have Jay come rescue her which just makes me love him more.<br /><br />The Storyline<br /><br />Like I mentioned above the basic storyline is pretty predictable and I thought it was easy to figure out who the stalker was but I enjoyed the new twist of Sara and Rafe, apparent independent crime consultants who use unusual means to solve cases. It sets up nicely for future adventures if Violet decides she wants to work with them or even to see what they do if Violet decides not to work with them. I am also curious to see what kind of guy Rafe turns out to be.<br /><br />This is definitely another great read from Kimberly Derting.</span>

<div id="review_122626816" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122626816" />
    <a title="Leah  (Simply Nerdy Book Reviews)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2172285-leah-simply-nerdy-book-reviews"><img alt="Leah  (Simply Nerdy Book Reviews)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344316660p2/2172285.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122626816?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leah  (Simply Nerdy Book Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah  (Simply Nerdy Book Reviews)" href="/user/show/2172285-leah-simply-nerdy-book-reviews">Leah  (Simply Nerdy Book Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122626816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer869620302091268922">I loved loved loved this book! Just as with its predecessor, Desires of the Dead is stunning on all counts. It's romantic, mysterious, suspenseful, funny, and very creative. Kimberly Derting'swriting is so fantastic, and her characters all so three-dimensional with such different and pronounced personalties that they, the plot, and the books themselves are so completely unforgettable.<br/><br/>Violet comes off just as strong as before, and her eerie ability becomes even more eerie in this novel, when it b</span>
  <span id="freeText869620302091268922" style="display:none">I loved loved loved this book! Just as with its predecessor, Desires of the Dead is stunning on all counts. It's romantic, mysterious, suspenseful, funny, and very creative. Kimberly Derting'swriting is so fantastic, and her characters all so three-dimensional with such different and pronounced personalties that they, the plot, and the books themselves are so completely unforgettable.<br /><br />Violet comes off just as strong as before, and her eerie ability becomes even more eerie in this novel, when it begins to involve characters closer to her and Jay. Violet's choice of working for someone, using her ability purposely to find murdered people and their killers, was easy to sympathize with--could you really tell someone something you'd spent your entire life keeping a secret, if it would benefit others? Even if it was something as dark as Violet's ability?<br /><br />Jay is so sweet and protective--the ideal boyfriend/best friend--that you just have to love him, and I swear, I'm more in love with him than Violet is. The normal (well, semi-normal; most of us don't have to deal with the prospect of murderers coming and killing us,) issues that him and Violet face help with building the strong romantic focus, make their relationship very realistic and paced just right, unlike quite a few other young adult fiction novels of today.<br /><br />I have to say, Derting does a fantastic job--even better, I think, than Kiersten White (author of Paranormalcy)--with supporting character development. My favorite character, actually, is Chelsea, Violet's closest girl friend. She's absolutely hilarious, and definitely has the most memorable personality in the two books. She's just so snarky and witty; I completely adore her! Claire is so sweet an innocent, too, that it just makes me laugh.<br /><br />As with the first book, I really enjoyed the brief chapters in the supposed "killer"'s perspective, because you feel connected with her on a certain level, and sympathize with her emotions and the circumstances in which she lives . . . you can almost understand why she does the things she does. This adds to the book's suspense, because, in some ways, you almost wish that what it's telling you is wrong--she cant really be the killer, can she? This aspect of the book was very unpredictable, because you never really knew--not until the very, very end.<br /><br />The seeds of doubt the events in the book planted in my mind drove me crazy with suspense and kept me reading until late at night, unable to stop. The romance reels you in from the very start, and the suspense doesn't let you go. I read for hours on end, staying up as late as I could, putting my homework aside, all along not even realizing how fast I sped through it, how quickly I passed each chapter mark. All in all, Desires of the Dead is another masterpiece by Kimberly Derting!<br /><br />These books would be fantastic for fans of the 1-800-WHERE-R-YOU series by Meg Cabot, Melissa Marr's stunning Wicked Lovely novels, and the Darkest Powers series by Kelley Armstrong.<br /><br />SIMPLY NERDY BOOK REVIEWS<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.simplynerdy.com">www.simplynerdy.com</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="869620302091268922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_164155423" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/164155423" />
    <a title="Tess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4595593-tess"><img alt="Tess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291635873p2/4595593.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/164155423?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tess" href="/user/show/4595593-tess">Tess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164155423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12681777957135152691">I remember reading The Body Finder and loving it, especially the budding romance between Violet and her childhood friend Jay, which was truly sweet. And so, when this sequel hit the shelves, I knew I wanted to continue their story.<br/><br/>Hence, here I am a few chapters in. Violet and Jay are now a couple, and as much in love as before. But troubles are closing in, and it comes from various directions.<br/><br/>Firstly, there are two new kids in school, Mike and his sister, and Jay has started to spend far too mu</span>
  <span id="freeText12681777957135152691" style="display:none">I remember reading The Body Finder and loving it, especially the budding romance between Violet and her childhood friend Jay, which was truly sweet. And so, when this sequel hit the shelves, I knew I wanted to continue their story.<br /><br />Hence, here I am a few chapters in. Violet and Jay are now a couple, and as much in love as before. But troubles are closing in, and it comes from various directions.<br /><br />Firstly, there are two new kids in school, Mike and his sister, and Jay has started to spend far too much time with Mike, to Violet’s dismay. Meanwhile, someone – a girl – is feeling angry with Violet for supposedly taking Jay from her and has started threatening Violet with various anonymous messages.<br /><br />As if that wasn’t all, Violet has also found a new body. As you may recall from The Body Finder, Violet has the uncanny ability to sense murdered bodies, as they give out a special echo sound that only Violet can hear. Once discovering a body, the echo will keep bugging Violet until it has been given a proper burial-place where it can rest in peace.<br /><br />Hence, after coming across this latest body, she places an anonymous call to the police so that it can be found. Problem is, her call is traced back to her, and before she knows it, the FBI has approached her for questioning. What will happen when they find out about her ability?<br /><br />And this is as far as I’ve got.<br /><br />Unfortunately, I have to admit I’m not feeling it yet with this sequel. Violet has started to bug me, because she keeps everything a secret, refuses to let anyone help her and in general is just too meek, quiet and gloomy for my liking. I’ve wanted to yell “get it together!” quite a few times already. Which can’t be a good sign. I’m especially frustrated with the way Violet treats Jay, who does everything in his power to keep her happy, yet all she does is pouts.<br /><br />Moreover, the plot is not much of a plot yet, rather it’s screaming filler. Particularly the subplot about a psycho girl who dumps dead cats on Violet’s porch is a bit too over the top for me. It sounds more like Glen Close in Fatal Attraction than a little school girl who is jealous over another girl’s boyfriend, don’t you think?<br /><br />In short, I’m trying to remember now what was so good with The Body Finder, because doubts are creeping in. Or maybe I’m being too harsh here, it may get better the more I read, let’s hope so..<br /><br />Full review at:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://readingaftertwilight.wordpress.com/2011/04/28/desires-of-the-dead-by-kimberly-derting/">http://readingaftertwilight.wordpress...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12681777957135152691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_139949003" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139949003" />
    <a title="Brianna (The Book Vixen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2125148-brianna-the-book-vixen"><img alt="Brianna (The Book Vixen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1377917104p2/2125148.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139949003?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brianna (The Book Vixen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brianna (The Book Vixen)" href="/user/show/2125148-brianna-the-book-vixen">Brianna (The Book Vixen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2125148-brianna-the-book-vixen?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2125148-brianna-the-book-vixen?shelf=_cb">_cb</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139949003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16770088267919036434"><b>Why I Read this Book:</b> When I finally got a hold of and read <i>The Body Finder</i>, I was pleased to find out that the things I heard about the book were true. It truly is a great debut novel. I was expecting a cliffhanger ending at the end of The Body Finder but there wasn’t one.Why was I expecting one? I’m not exactly sure. Maybe because it’s a series that involves the same main characters with a continuing storyline. And while all loose ends were tied by the end, I was still interested in reading <i>De</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16770088267919036434" style="display:none"><b>Why I Read this Book:</b> When I finally got a hold of and read <i>The Body Finder</i>, I was pleased to find out that the things I heard about the book were true. It truly is a great debut novel. I was expecting a cliffhanger ending at the end of The Body Finder but there wasn’t one.Why was I expecting one? I’m not exactly sure. Maybe because it’s a series that involves the same main characters with a continuing storyline. And while all loose ends were tied by the end, I was still interested in reading <i>Desires of the Dead</i> to find out what else was going on with Violet.<br /><br /><b>What I Liked:</b> As with <i>The Body Finder</i>, I was invested in the author’s writing style. The descriptions were vivid enough without being too drawn out. Also like it’s predecessor, <i>Desires of the Dead</i> included brief chapters that gives the reader an idea of what’s going on inside the antagonist’s mind. This actually threw me off, not at first but about in the middle of the book. You think you know who the antagonist is but then something comes up, leaving you not so sure.<br /><br />I liked that the prologue is an event that takes place towards the end of the book and the book leads the reader to that point. The prologue definitely pulled me right in. You will want to devour <i>Desires of the Dead</i> in one sitting.<br /><br /><b>What I Didn’t Like:</b> I can’t believe Violet was so untrusting of Jay, unlike her relationship with him in <i>The Body Finder</i>. And Chelsea is getting on my nerves now, big time. She’s too selfish and self-serving. I wanted to smack her silly.<br /><br /><b>Overall Impression:</b> <i>Desires of the Dead</i> is a good follow-up novel. I feel that this book was up to par with the first; neither of the two books outshone the other. Towards the end of this book, I was a little concerned about how things were going to be wrapped up but the author pulled through and did a fabulous job. Most loose ends were tied up so there was no major cliffhanger. There was just enough of the storyline left open to get me interested in reading the next book. There’s definitely room to expand on this series and I cannot wait to see where the author takes the storyline next with the next 2 books. The story arc involving Sara seems interesting and I’m curious to see where the author takes it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16770088267919036434" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_93641176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/93641176" />
    <a title="Princess Bookie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1218813-princess-bookie"><img alt="Princess Bookie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1243916881p2/1218813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/93641176?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Princess Bookie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Princess Bookie" href="/user/show/1218813-princess-bookie">Princess Bookie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1218813-princess-bookie?shelf=read2010">read2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer93641176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4430948296156034494"><br/>My Thoughts: Once again we are back with Violet and her hectic abilities. Remember, from The Body Finder we found out she can hear echoes from dead people, the ones who died; murdered. It isn't just people she can hear, she can also hear animals. She can also sense the people who committed the crime since the imprint attaches to them. Creepy? Yes! Useful? Sometimes! Violet is trying to adjust to life just being herself and spending time with Jay. She was always so used to having him as her best </span>
  <span id="freeText4430948296156034494" style="display:none"><br />My Thoughts: Once again we are back with Violet and her hectic abilities. Remember, from The Body Finder we found out she can hear echoes from dead people, the ones who died; murdered. It isn't just people she can hear, she can also hear animals. She can also sense the people who committed the crime since the imprint attaches to them. Creepy? Yes! Useful? Sometimes! Violet is trying to adjust to life just being herself and spending time with Jay. She was always so used to having him as her best friend, now they are adjusting to being boyfriend and girlfriend! There is a new guy and girl in town, siblings. Jay befriends them and we get to know their family history and a little about them.<br /><br />Of course Violet can't get away from the imprints, she hears one and calls the police. Come to find out, someone was in the place she heard it. And the FBI tracked down Violet from her phone call. Now the FBI wants to work with her. There is also a boy about her age working for the FBI.<br /><br />We also get to read a few pages here and there from the other narrator just like we did in The Body Finder. It was very interesting to hear their opinion. <br /><br />What can I say? I really loved Desires Of The Dead. I read it in one sitting late at night. It's a bit creepy but in a good way. I still love Jay but I found myself drawn to the new boy and his special "talent." I hope to learn more about him in future books. <br /><br />Someone is also stalking Violet. They leave her a dead cat, a note, and they overall stalk her. There is also the mystery of where the new kids mother went. That is what the book mainly focuses on. <br /><br />I won't say much more or else there won't be any reason for you to read the book! <br /><br />Kimberly Derting knows how to suck you in, satisfy you while reading, and leave you wanting more! <br /><br />Overall: I loved Desires Of The Dead. I loved it just as much as The Body Finder and I really loved The Body Finder! I did like the plot a little better in The Body Finder but I also liked this one as well! <br /><br />Cover: I love the pink cover more than I did the blue! Very artistic! <br /><br />What I'd Give It: 5/5 Cupcakes<br /><br />________________________________<br />Review Based On Hardcover Edition<br /><br />Taken from Princess Bookie<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.princessbookie.com">www.princessbookie.com</a></span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fajZZ59/RBa9JxUZ3tI5ABRafe8JfdzXU8/x+LyWFjLrLcMgGI/wOAKV8xGkuZiTtn/begBVJc9fbOpKSo+HVg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('I04EEWLtWvMM6LVrt02FQJNhU6jbfyM2gKKNsm9SmvW1yx5W5R3u3bNaU2PNJiTTMUT1PdJX2i6MAZYAmUsLkQ==')})
  }
//]]>
